2:34:2541:0:14:71:498:708:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Employer Matching and 401(k) Saving: Evidence From the Health and Retirement Study
2:35:2623:14:14:71:246:694:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Gary V. Engelhardt and Anil Kumar
2:36:2656:14:14:71:232:680:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:NBER Working Paper No. 12447
2:37:2684:14:14:71:133:666:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:August 2006
2:38:2695:14:29:71:183:652:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:JEL No. E21, H24, J32
2:39:2716:29:42:273:338:623:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:F:ABSTRACT
2:40:2724:42:14:71:539:581:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Employer matching of employee 401(k) contributions can provide a powerful incentive to save for
2:41:2819:14:15:71:539:567:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:retirement  and  is  a  key  component  in  pension-plan  design  in  the  United  States.    Using  detailed
2:42:2928:15:14:71:539:552:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:administrative contribution, earnings, and pension-plan data from the Health and Retirement Study,
2:43:3026:14:14:71:539:538:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:this  analysis  formulates  a  life-cycle-consistent  econometric  specification  of  401(k)  saving  and
2:44:3131:14:14:71:539:524:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:estimates  the  determinants  of  saving  accounting  for  non-linearities  in  the  household  budget  set
2:45:3238:14:14:71:539:510:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:induced by matching.  The participation estimates indicate that an increase in the match rate by 25
2:46:3337:14:14:71:539:496:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:cents per dollar of employee contribution raises 401(k) participation by 3.75 to 6 percentage points,
2:47:3438:14:15:71:539:482:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:and the estimated elasticity of participation with respect to matching ranges from 0.02-0.07.  The
2:48:3536:15:14:71:539:467:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:parametric and semi-parametric estimates for saving indicate that an increase in the match rate by
2:49:3634:14:14:71:539:453:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:25 cents per dollar of employee contribution raises 401(k) saving by $400-$700 (in 1991 dollars).
2:50:3731:14:14:71:539:439:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:The  estimated  elasticity  of  401(k)  saving  to  matching  is  also  small  and  ranges  from  0.09-0.12
2:51:3838:14:14:71:539:425:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:overall, with just under half of this effect on the intensive margin.  Overall, the analysis reveals that
2:52:3943:14:43:71:462:411:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:matching is a rather poor policy instrument with which to raise retirement saving.
2:53:4025:43:14:71:165:368:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Gary V. Engelhardt
2:54:4043:14:14:71:200:354:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Center for Policy Research
2:55:4069:14:14:71:149:340:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:423 Eggers Hall
2:56:4084:14:14:71:167:326:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Syracuse University
2:57:4103:14:14:71:198:312:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Syracuse, NY 13244-1020

3:61:4159:13:28:90:176:697:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:I. Introduction 
3:62:4174:28:27:126:526:669:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:As  401(k)s  have  come  to  dominate  the  private  pension  landscape  in  the  United  
3:63:4264:27:28:90:525:642:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:States, researchers and policy makers have given increased attention to the impact of plan 
3:64:4355:28:27:90:525:614:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics  on  retirement-saving  decisions.1    One  important  characteristic  is  whether  
3:65:4455:27:28:90:525:587:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and to what extent the employer matches employee contributions.  A typical match might 
3:66:4542:28:28:90:526:559:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:be  50  cents  for  each  dollar  of  contribution,  up  to  a  maximum  percentage  of  pay,  say,  6  
3:67:4646:28:27:90:527:531:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent.    Although  much  of  the  discussion  by  the  popular  press  and  policy  makers  
3:68:4741:27:28:90:526:504:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:presumes  employer  matching  raises  saving,  there  is  actually  strikingly  little  consensus  
3:69:4840:28:27:89:525:476:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:among researchers.  Some studies have found that increases in the match rate raise 401(k) 
3:70:4930:27:28:89:526:449:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:saving  (Papke  and  Poterba,  1995;  Clark  and  Schieber,  1998;  VanDerhei  and  Copeland,  
3:71:5025:28:28:89:525:421:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:2001; and Choi, Laibson, Madrian, and Metrick, 2002).  Others have found that it is not 
3:72:5113:28:27:89:526:393:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  match  rate  per  se  that  matters,  but  whether  the  firm  offers  a  match  at  all  (Even  and  
3:73:5220:27:28:89:525:366:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Macpherson, 1996; Bassett, Fleming, and Rodrigues, 1998; Papke, 1995; Kusko, Poterba, 
3:74:5306:28:27:89:526:338:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and  Wilcox,  1998).    That  is,  providing  a  match  raises  401(k)  saving,  but  an  increase  in  
3:75:5410:27:28:89:526:311:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  level  of  the  match  rate  (conditional  on  providing  a  match)  does  not.    Finally,  still  
3:76:5515:28:28:89:527:283:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:other  studies  (Employee  Benefit  Research  Institute,  1994;  Andrews,  1992;  Munnell,  
3:77:5607:28:27:89:526:255:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Sunden,  and  Taylor,  1998;  and  GAO,  1997)  have  suggested  that,  conditional  on  being  
3:78:5703:27:28:89:526:228:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:eligible  for  a  match,  an  increase  in  the  match  rate  lowers  401(k)  contributions,  which,  
3:79:5805:28:27:89:525:200:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:when interpreted in the context of a simple two-period model of saving, suggests that the 
3:80:5895:27:53:89:526:173:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:income  effect  dominates  the  substitution  effect  from  the  higher  rate  of  return  matching  
3:81:5996:53:7:89:237:120:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
3:82:6044:7:16:90:526:113:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:1  This  includes  work  on  automatic  enrollment  (Madrian  and  Shea,  2001;  Choi,  Laibson,  Madrian,  and  
3:83:6157:16:12:90:525:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Metrick, 2002, 2004), investment in company stock (Poterba, 2003; Brown, Liang, and Weisbenner, 2004; 
3:84:6259:12:11:90:524:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Mitchell and Utkus, 2002), portfolio choice and trading in 401(k) plans (Benartzi and Thaler, 2001; Agnew, 
3:85:6366:11:0:90:216:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Balduzzi, and Sunden, 2003).   
4:86:6398:0:27:90:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:provides.2    Overall,  this  ambiguity  has  emerged  as  an  important  empirical  puzzle  in  the  
4:87:6500:27:28:89:327:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:literature on saving behavior (Bernheim, 2003).   
4:88:6550:28:27:125:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:A central shortcoming in this literature has been the failure to exploit the fact that 
4:89:6637:27:28:89:528:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer  matching,  based  either  on  multiple-match-rate  schedules  or  caps  on  the  
4:90:6728:28:28:89:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:generosity  of  the  match,  results  in  a  non-linear household budget set.  As has been long 
4:91:6824:28:27:90:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:recognized in the study of taxation on labor supply, reduced-form estimates of behavioral 
4:92:6914:27:28:90:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:elasticities are biased and inconsistent unless the non-linearity is accounted for explicitly 
4:93:7008:28:27:90:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(Hausman, 1985; Moffitt, 1990; Blundell and MaCurdy, 1999).  Indeed, the presence of 
4:94:7093:27:28:90:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:budget-set kinks may reconcile some of the findings of previous studies: for example, the 
4:95:7183:28:28:90:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:provision  of  a  match  may  raise  401(k)  saving  if  the  substitution  effect  dominates,  but  
4:96:7284:28:27:90:454:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:variation in match rates may not matter if employees are bunched at kinks.  
4:97:7360:27:28:90:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: Unlike previous studies, this paper includes a detailed theoretical framework that 
4:98:7443:28:27:90:526:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:models  the  budget  set  defined  by  employer  matching  and  federal  tax  treatment  as  twice  
4:99:7543:27:28:90:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:continuously  differentiable  and  then  uses  the  first-order  conditions  from  the  consumer’s  
4:100:7643:28:27:90:529:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:optimization   to   derive   a   life-cycle-consistent   econometric   specification   for   401(k)   
4:101:7745:27:28:90:526:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participation.    As  an  alternative  to  the  maximum-likelihood  piecewise-linear-budget-set  
4:102:7842:28:28:89:528:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:estimation  summarized  in  Hausman  (1985)—and  the  recent,  related  non-parametric  
4:103:7930:28:27:89:534:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:extensions    by    Blomquist    and    Newey    (2002)—and    the    maximum    likelihood    
4:104:8025:27:28:89:526:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:differentiable-budget-constraint  methodology  of  MaCurdy,  Green,  and  Paarsch  (1990),  
4:105:8117:28:27:89:526:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:this  paper  employs  instrumental-variable  techniques  that  linearize  the  budget  set  at  the  
4:106:8218:27:28:89:524:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:observed outcome to calculate the price and virtual-income terms and then instruments to 
4:107:8307:28:20:89:525:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:correct for endogeneity, which also has a long history, but a recent example of which is 
4:108:8396:20:8:89:237:109:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
4:109:8444:8:16:90:525:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:2 Throughout the paper, “401(k) saving” and “401(k) contributions” are used synonymously as per period 
4:110:8547:16:11:90:524:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:flows.  In a multi-period model, this would suggest the income effect dominates the substitution and wealth 
4:111:8655:11:0:90:199:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:effects (Summers, 1981).   
5:112:8683:0:27:90:527:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Ziliak  and  Kniesner  (1999).      To  calculate  budget-set  slopes  and  virtual  income  in  a  
5:113:8783:27:28:90:522:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhood around kink points, kernel regression is used to smooth the budget set non-
5:114:8871:28:27:89:527:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:parametrically.    We  also  estimate  a  censored  regression  model  of  401(k)  saving  to  
5:115:8966:27:28:90:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:decompose  the  overall  401(k)  saving  response  between  the  extensive  and  the  intensive  
5:116:9063:28:28:90:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:margin, where the instrumental-variable Tobit estimator of Newey (1986, 1987b) and an 
5:117:9149:28:27:90:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:instrumental-variable  symmetrically  censored  least  squares  (SCLS)  estimator  based  on  
5:118:9243:27:28:90:299:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Powell (1986) and Newey (1986) are used. 
5:119:9284:28:27:90:526:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:  Empirically,  the  paper  makes  four  additional  contributions.    First,  to  circumvent  
5:120:9379:27:28:90:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:difficulties with measurement error in 401(k) contributions and matching incentives that 
5:121:9468:28:28:90:529:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have   plagued   previous   studies,   administrative   data   from   three   sources   are   used:   
5:122:9570:28:27:90:525:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contributions from W-2 earnings records provided by the Social Security Administration 
5:123:9657:27:28:90:527:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(SSA)  and  Internal  Revenue  Service  (IRS);    detailed  matching  formulas  from  pension  
5:124:9752:28:27:90:526:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Summary Plan Descriptions (SPD) provided by the employers of Health and Retirement 
5:125:9835:27:28:90:530:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Study   (HRS)   respondents;   and,   a   combination   of   Social-Security-covered-earnings   
5:126:9931:28:27:90:521:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:histories  for  1951-1991  and  W-2  earnings  for  1980-1991,  pension  SPDs,  and  pension-
5:127:10024:27:28:90:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:benefit calculators to construct public and private pension entitlements and accruals.  The 
5:128:10116:28:28:90:531:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sample  consists  of  1,042  individuals  in  1991  eligible  for  401(k)  plans  in  the  HRS.    
5:129:10215:28:27:90:527:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Second,  the  analysis  includes  a  calculation  of  the  dollar  amount  of  unused  employer  
5:130:10312:27:28:90:527:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:matching  contributions  due  to  workers’  failure  to  contribute  at  least  until  the  point  at  
5:131:10415:28:27:90:522:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:which   the   employer   match   is   exhausted.      Most   of   this   occurs   because   of   non-
5:132:10516:27:28:89:528:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participation.    For  non-participants,  the  unclaimed  employer  match  represented  3.7  
5:133:10609:28:28:89:525:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent of pay.  However, even participants left “money on the table” equal to 1 percent 
5:134:10698:28:0:90:525:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of pay in unclaimed employer match.  Based on measures of liquidity constraints used by 
6:135:10787:0:27:90:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:others  in  the  literature,  reduced-form  evidence  is  not  inconsistent  with  the  presence  of  
6:136:10889:27:28:90:528:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:liquidity  constraints  as  a  potential  explanation  for  this  phenomenon.    Third,  unlike  
6:137:10986:28:27:90:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:previous pension studies that have used the employer-provided SPDs in the HRS, which 
6:138:11071:27:28:90:525:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:are available only for a non-random sub-sample of HRS respondents, the estimation uses 
6:139:11158:28:28:90:527:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:methods  laid  out  in  Vella  (1992)  and  Das,  Newey,  and  Vella  (2003)  to  correct  for  
6:140:11254:28:27:90:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:potential  sample  selection  using  a  set  of  plausible  exclusion  restrictions  derived  from  
6:141:11354:27:28:90:527:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Internal  Revenue  Service  (IRS)  Form  5500  administrative  pension-plan  filings.    The  
6:142:11448:28:27:90:527:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:exclusions  have  substantial  predictive  power  for  determining  who  is  in  the  analysis  
6:143:11544:27:28:90:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sample.  There is statistically significant evidence of selection, but the economic impact 
6:144:11635:28:28:90:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  selection  on  the  estimates  is  mixed:  the  bias  is  small  in  the  censored  regression  
6:145:11740:28:27:90:530:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:specifications  of  saving,  but  larger  in  the  discrete  choice  participation  specifications.    
6:146:11843:27:28:90:527:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Finally,  there  is  substantial  evidence  of  the  bunching  of  401(k)  contributions  around  
6:147:11941:28:27:90:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:budget-set kink points induced by employer matching: about 25 percent of match-eligible 
6:148:12029:27:28:90:264:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:individuals are bunched at the kink. 
6:149:12066:28:27:90:533:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:    The    estimates    from    the    life-cycle-consistent    discrete    choice    regression    
6:150:12166:27:28:90:526:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:specifications  for  participation  indicate  that  the  estimated  marginal  effect  of  an  increase  
6:151:12270:28:28:90:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in the employer match rate by 25 cents per dollar of employee contribution raises 401(k) 
6:152:12359:28:27:90:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participation by 3.75 to 6 percentage points.  When the estimates are expressed in terms 
6:153:12448:27:28:90:525:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of elasticities, the results suggest that the impact of the match rate on 401(k) participation 
6:154:12543:28:27:90:524:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is quite inelastic: the estimated elasticity of 401(k) participation with respect to the match 
6:155:12638:27:28:89:526:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rate  ranges  from  0.02-0.07.    In  addition,  the  parametric  and  semi-parametric  estimates  
6:156:12737:28:28:89:525:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:from the two-limit censored regression specifications indicate that the estimated marginal 
6:157:12828:28:0:89:527:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:effect  of  an  increase  in  the  employer  match  rate  by  25  cents  per  dollar  of  employee  
7:158:12929:0:27:90:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contribution  raises  401(k)  contributions  by  $400-$700  dollars  (in  constant  calendar  year  
7:159:13029:27:28:90:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1991 dollars).  Comparing the Tobit and SCLS estimates using the Hausman-type test in 
7:160:13115:28:27:90:527:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Newey  (1987a),  the  validity  of  the  Tobit  model  cannot  be  rejected.    When  the  Tobit  
7:161:13213:27:28:90:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:estimates are expressed in terms of elasticities, the results suggest that the impact of the 
7:162:13306:28:28:90:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:match  rate  on  401(k)  saving  is  quite  inelastic:  the  estimated  elasticity  of  401(k)  saving  
7:163:13410:28:27:90:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with respect to the match rate ranges from 0.09-0.12 overall, with just under one half of 
7:164:13500:27:28:90:479:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:this effect on the intensive (contributions conditional on participation) margin.    
7:165:13585:28:27:90:527:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:  Overall,  because  of  this  very  inelastic  response  on  both  the  intensive  and  the  
7:166:13679:27:28:90:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:extensive margins, the analysis reveals that for employers and policy makers interested in 
7:167:13770:28:28:90:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:promoting  retirement  saving  by  older  workers  through  greater  401(k)  participation  and  
7:168:13867:28:27:90:527:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:saving,  matching  is  a  rather  poor  policy  instrument.    Roughly  speaking,  the  estimated  
7:169:13966:27:28:90:526:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:marginal  effects  in  this  paper  suggest  that  an  increase  in  the  employer  match  rate  of  $1  
7:170:14071:28:27:90:528:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:per  $1  of  employee  contribution  would  be  needed  to  achieve  the  same  increase  in  
7:171:14165:27:28:90:527:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participation  as  the  implementation  of  automatic  enrollment,  based  on  the  estimates  in  
7:172:14264:28:27:90:525:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Madrian and Shea (2001) and Choi, Laibson, Madrian, and Metrick (2002, 2004).   The 
7:173:14348:27:28:90:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:analysis also suggests that government matching of voluntary contributions to any type of 
7:174:14438:28:28:89:521:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Social  Security  personal  account  would  be  relatively  ineffective  in  promoting  personal-
7:175:14535:28:27:89:349:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:account contributions (Engelhardt and Kumar, 2005). 
7:176:14587:27:28:125:526:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The  paper  is  organized  as  follows.    Sections  II  and  III  lay  out  the  theoretical  
7:177:14682:28:27:89:526:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:model  and  first-order  conditions  that  directly  motivates  the  empirical  analysis.    Section  
7:178:14784:27:28:89:525:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:IV lays out the econometric framework and construction of the key variables.  Sections V 
7:179:14873:28:28:89:524:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and VI describe the data.  Section VII describes the empirical analysis of the relationship 
7:180:14965:28:0:89:526:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:between  matching  and  measures  of  liquidity  constraints.    For  purposes  of  comparison  
8:181:15062:0:27:90:527:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with  our  more  structural  approach,  Section  VIII  presents  estimation  results  for  ad  hoc  
8:182:15162:27:28:90:528:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:reduced-form  specification  similar  to  those  in  the  previous  literature.    Section  IX  
8:183:15258:28:27:90:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:discusses the identification of the structural model, and section X presents the estimation 
8:184:15350:27:28:90:264:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:results.  There is a brief conclusion. 
8:185:15389:28:28:126:135:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:   
8:186:15392:28:27:90:233:570:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:II. Theoretical Framework 
8:187:15417:27:28:126:528:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Previous  studies  have  had  two  important  shortcomings.    First,  they  have  not  
8:188:15505:28:27:90:526:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:couched  their  analyses  in  formal  models  of  intertemporal  choice,  even  though  saving  
8:189:15601:27:28:90:527:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:involves  the  substitution  of  resources  across  time.    This  means  that  previous  estimates  
8:190:15702:28:28:90:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cannot  be  interpreted  as  estimates  of  life-cycle-consistent  determinants  of  401(k)  saving  
8:191:15803:28:27:90:528:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:necessarily,  because  the  empirical  specifications  may  not  have  been  consistent  with  
8:192:15898:27:28:90:527:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:underlying  utility  maximization.    So,  while  the  existing  literature  has  provided  quite  
8:193:15997:28:27:90:526:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:informative descriptive analyses, it has said little about how 401(k) saving may respond 
8:194:16086:27:28:90:524:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to prospective changes in employer matching or what the optimal match rate should be to 
8:195:16174:28:27:90:527:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:achieve  a  saving  target.  Second,  with  the  exception  of  Choi,  Laibson,  Madrian,  and  
8:196:16270:27:28:90:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Metrick (2002), Mitchell, Utkus, and Yang (2005), and VanDerhei and Copeland (2001), 
8:197:16355:28:28:90:526:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:previous  studies  have  failed  to  exploit  the  fact  that  multiple-match-rate  schedules  and  
8:198:16455:28:27:90:334:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f4:B:caps on matching induce kinks in the budget set.    
8:199:16506:27:28:90:528:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:  By  specifying  a  detailed  theoretical  framework,  this  paper  represents  a  stark  
8:200:16597:28:27:90:524:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:departure from the previous literature.  In an effort to shorten the exposition, the model is 
8:201:16691:27:28:90:512:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:presented in full in Appendix A and briefly summarized here.  It has nine key features:  
8:202:16780:28:19:108:529:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:1) Intratemporal   direct   utility,   );,(zlCU,   is   derived   from   leisure,   l,   with   an   
8:203:16880:19:19:126:526:110:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:associated  price,  lp,  consumption  of  a  composite  good,C,  with  an  associated  
8:204:16967:19:16:126:528:91:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:price, cp,  and  a  vector  of  demographics,  z,  and  is  intratemporally  weakly  
8:205:17052:16:0:126:376:75:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:separable and intertemporally additively separable.  
9:206:17106:0:14:108:111:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
9:207:17106:14:16:108:524:694:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:2) The  consumer  faces  a  per  period  probability  of  survival  of  ρ,  with  period  T 
9:208:17196:16:19:125:528:678:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:being  the  known  maximum  length  of  life,  and  with  probability  ρ−1, the 
9:209:17276:19:19:126:526:659:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:consumer  dies  and  receives  the  terminal  payoff  )(TWΦ,  the  utility  of  bequests,  
9:210:17367:19:14:126:327:640:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:which is a function of total wealth, TW.   
9:211:17410:14:14:90:93:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
9:212:17410:14:14:108:524:612:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:3) The lifetime is composed of two parts: from periodNtoΤ, the consumer is retired 
9:213:17492:14:14:125:527:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:and  no  hours  of  labor  are  supplied  to  the  market,  so  leisure  equals  the  time  
9:214:17584:14:14:125:527:584:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:endowment,  and  from  period  0  to 1-N,  the  consumer  works;  the  timing  of  
9:215:17666:14:14:126:320:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:retirement in period N is endogenous.   
9:216:17706:14:14:90:93:556:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
9:217:17706:14:14:107:522:542:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:4) Total  wealth  is  accumulated  in  seven  forms  when  working:  IRAs,  401(k)s,  non-
9:218:17795:14:13:126:528:528:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:401(k)  defined-contribution  (DC)  pension  plans,  defined-benefit  (DB)  pension  
9:219:17880:13:14:126:415:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:plans, Social Security, housing equity, and taxable wealth.   
9:220:17942:14:14:89:92:501:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
9:221:17942:14:14:107:526:487:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:5) Retirement-account  wealth,  defined  as  the  sum  of  IRA,  401(k),  and  non-401(k)  
9:222:18032:14:16:126:527:473:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:DC  assets,  and  taxable  wealth  can  be  invested  in  risky  stocks,  with  stochastic  
9:223:18124:16:14:125:527:457:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:return sr,  and  riskless  bonds,  and,  in  addition  to  the  optimal  asset  allocation  
9:224:18216:14:14:125:524:443:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:decision  across  the  different  forms  of  wealth,  there  is  an  optimal  asset  location 
9:225:18309:14:14:125:526:429:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:decision, whereby the consumer must decide which assets to hold in taxable and 
9:226:18388:14:14:125:227:415:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:tax-deferred forms.   
9:227:18410:14:13:89:92:401:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
9:228:18410:13:14:107:529:388:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:6) The  model  specifies  in  detail  non-linearities  in  the  budget  set  induced  by  
9:229:18499:14:14:126:530:374:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:employer   matching,   the   tax   treatment   of   401(k)   and   IRA   contributions,   
9:230:18589:14:14:126:527:360:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:respectively,  IRA  withdrawals,  including  the  tax  penalty  for  early  withdrawals  
9:231:18678:14:14:126:531:346:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:and   minimum-distribution   requirements,   and   the   interrelationship   between   
9:232:18765:14:13:126:480:332:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:employer matching, 401(k) plan characteristics, and the price of leisure.   
9:233:18841:13:14:89:92:319:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
9:234:18841:14:14:107:526:305:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:7) There  are  four  liquidity  constraints:  a)  non-401(k)-DC,  DB  and  Social  Security  
9:235:18933:14:14:126:526:291:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:wealth  are  assumed  illiquid  until  retirement  and  cannot  be  used  as  collateral  (in  
9:236:19028:14:14:126:525:277:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:accordance with federal law); b) there are constraints on the housing loan-to-value 
9:237:19112:14:13:126:525:263:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:ratio for homeowners which limits the amount of mortgage debt that can be held; 
9:238:19192:13:14:126:521:250:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:c)  401(k)  wealth  is  assumed  illiquid  until  retirement;  and  d)  there  is  a  cash-on-
9:239:19286:14:14:126:525:236:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:hand constraint, such that total per period full expenditure (also referred to as “full 
9:240:19374:14:16:126:526:222:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:income”  in  the  two-stage  budgeting  literature),  y,  must  be  less  than  or  equal  to  
9:241:19469:16:14:125:526:206:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:total  net  cash  on  hand,  where  the  latter  is  defined  as  beginning-of-period  liquid  
9:242:19564:14:14:125:527:192:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:taxable  wealth  and  other  income  on  hand,  plus  the  market  value  of  the  leisure  
9:243:19656:14:14:125:526:178:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:endowment,  less  the  tax  liability,  plus  any  IRA  wealth  made  liquid  through  a  
9:244:19746:14:13:125:525:164:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:withdrawal, less any tax-deferred saving in the form of contributions to the 401(k) 
9:245:19830:13:14:125:172:151:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:and IRA. 
9:246:19839:14:14:89:92:137:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
9:247:19839:14:14:107:525:123:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:8) In  each  period  t,  there  are  minimum-  and  maximum-contribution  constraints  on  
9:248:19929:14:14:125:457:109:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:401(k)s and IRAs (with multipliers in square brackets), respectively, 
9:249:19999:14:17:89:92:95:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:

10:271:20486:14:14:90:93:538:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
10:272:20486:14:16:107:524:524:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:9) Each period when working, the consumer chooses consumption, leisure, voluntary 
10:273:20567:16:16:125:526:508:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:401(k)  contributions,  VOLQ,  IRA  contributions,  IRACQ,    IRA  withdrawals,  the  
10:274:20653:16:14:126:528:492:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:housing  loan-to-value  ratio,  and  the  shares  of  retirement-account  and  taxable  
10:275:20741:14:14:126:525:478:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:wealth held in risky stocks, respectively.  Each period when retired, the consumer 
10:276:20824:14:14:126:522:464:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:chooses  consumption,  IRA  contributions,  IRA  withdrawals,  the  housing  loan-to-
10:277:20909:14:14:126:468:450:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:value ratio, and receives eligible pension and Social Security benefits.  
10:278:20983:14:13:108:111:436:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
10:279:20983:13:28:90:528:423:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:  To  summarize,  the  only  forms  of  “active”  saving  when  working  are  through  
10:280:21070:28:28:90:522:395:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contributions to 401(k), IRA, or taxable assets; adjustments can be made to the mortgage-
10:281:21159:28:27:90:526:367:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:debt position as well.  However, the primary technology for smoothing resources across 
10:282:21246:27:28:90:526:340:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:periods when working is through taxable-asset saving, because 401(k) saving is illiquid; 
10:283:21335:28:27:90:526:312:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:IRA contributions are not necessarily illiquid because of the availability of withdrawals, 
10:284:21426:27:28:90:525:285:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:but IRA withdrawals may incur a tax penalty; traditional pensions and Social Security are 
10:285:21516:28:28:90:525:257:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:illiquid; and the extent of mortgage borrowing is limited.  This means that the consumer’s 
10:286:21607:28:27:90:526:229:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:optimization  does  not  imply  automatically  that  all  active  saving  be  allocated  first  to  the  
10:287:21712:27:28:90:526:202:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tax-preferred  asset  with  the  highest  net  return,  because,  in  the  face  of  uncertainty,  the  
10:288:21816:28:27:90:476:174:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consumer must balance the desire for a high return with the need for liquidity.    
10:289:21899:27:28:90:93:147:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
10:290:21899:28:0:90:237:119:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:III.   First-Order Conditions 
11:291:21930:0:27:126:527:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:As  explained  in  the  data  section  below,  consumption  and  hours  are  not  fully  
11:292:22019:27:28:89:528:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:observed  in  the  HRS,  so  that,  from  the  perspective  of  the  empirical  analysis,  it  is  
11:293:22118:28:28:89:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:desirable  to  work  with  the  indirect,  rather  than  the  direct,  utility  function.    Specifically,  
11:294:22226:28:30:89:527:625:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:let                );,(zpyV  be  the  intratemporal  indirect  utility  function.    It  takes  as  arguments  the  
11:295:22342:30:32:90:527:595:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:vector  of  prices  of  leisure  and  consumption,  p,  full  income,  y,  and  the  vector  of  
11:296:22439:32:31:90:526:563:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:demographics, z.    Following  Browning,  Deaton,  and  Irish  (1985),  let  )(*TttWV  be  the  
11:297:22535:31:28:89:528:532:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sum  of  current  and  future  expected  utility  based  on  total  wealth  in  period  t.    The  
11:298:22634:28:31:89:526:504:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:individual  makes  all  decisions  at  the  beginning  of  the  period,  based  on  the  information  
11:299:22736:31:31:89:527:473:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:set, tΩ,  after  which,  sris  realized,E  is  the  expectations  operator  conditional  on  the  
11:300:22834:31:30:90:306:442:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:information set, and β is the discount rate.   
11:301:22881:30:27:126:521:412:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The  optimization  is  expressed  in  terms  of  two-stage  budgeting.3      In  the  first-
11:302:22973:27:28:90:528:385:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:stage,  the  individual  chooses  full  income,  dis-saving  through  IRA  withdrawals,  the  
11:303:23067:28:27:90:525:357:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:mortgage-debt  position,  and  the  portfolio  allocations  to  stock  of  retirement-account  and  
11:304:23167:27:28:90:524:330:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:taxable  wealth,  and  must  allocate  total  “active”  saving  to  three  asset  categories─401(k), 
11:305:23268:28:28:90:525:302:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:IRA, and taxable wealth─to maximize the expected present discounted value of lifetime 
11:306:23354:28:27:90:527:274:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:indirect  utility.    In  the  second  stage,  optimal  full  income  in  each  period  is  allocated  
11:307:23457:27:28:90:470:247:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:statically between the goods that enter direct utility: consumption and leisure.   
11:308:23540:28:27:126:531:219:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The   first-order   conditions   when   working   for   401(k)   contributions,   IRA   
11:309:23628:27:83:90:335:192:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contributions, and full income can be expressed as

11:312:23834:16:11:90:522:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:model  assumes  strongly  intertemporally  and  weakly  intratemporally  separable  preferences,  so  that  a  two-

16:558:31745:28:28:90:526:331:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:but  may  affect  contributions.    In  the  baseline  specifications,  x  is  limited  to  a  constant;

16:560:31940:27:28:89:131:276:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:      
16:561:31946:28:27:90:145:248:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:V.   Data  
16:562:31956:27:28:90:527:221:100:Courier:144:g_d0_f3:B:   Previous  research  primarily  has  used  nationally  representative,  individual-level  
16:563:32047:28:27:90:527:193:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:survey  data,  such  as  the  Current  Population  Studies  (CPS)  and  Surveys  of  Consumer  
16:564:32142:27:28:90:531:166:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Finances  (SCF),  which  are  plagued  by  two  important  sources  of  measurement  error.    
16:565:32237:28:28:90:527:138:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:First,  even  though  the  researcher  must  know  the  entire  match  schedule  for  a  plan  to  
16:566:32336:28:27:90:528:110:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:account  for  the  individual’s  full  opportunity  set,  as  well  as  whether  the  match  is  
16:567:32433:27:0:90:526:83:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:discretionary or through profit-sharing, the typical survey respondent has great difficulty 
17:568:32527:0:27:90:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in accurately conveying even relatively simple pension provisions to interviewers, no less 
17:569:32618:27:28:90:526:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:detailed  matching  schedules.5    Second,  self-reported  contribution  data  also  suffer  from  
17:570:32717:28:27:90:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:substantial  reporting  error.    In  addition,  as  the  theoretical  framework  showed,  the  data  
17:571:32819:27:28:90:527:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:required  to  model  saving  are  quite  extensive:  contributions,  components  of  household  
17:572:32915:28:28:90:528:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(including  spousal)  income,  assets,  debts,  demographics,  marginal  tax  rates,  spousal  
17:573:33010:28:27:90:530:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:pension   coverage,   and   expected   entitlements   from   Social   Security   and   traditional   
17:574:33111:27:28:90:524:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:pensions, which require lifetime and job earnings histories, respectively.  Previous studies 
17:575:33204:28:27:90:242:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have not had all of these data.   
17:576:33238:27:28:126:527:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:In  this  paper,  these  problems  are  overcome  by  using  remarkably  detailed  data  
17:577:33327:28:28:90:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:from the first wave of the HRS, a nationally representative random sample of 51-61 year 
17:578:33415:28:27:90:525:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:olds and their spouses (regardless of age).  The first wave asked detailed questions about 
17:579:33506:27:28:90:526:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:wealth  (including  IRA  and  taxable  assets),  demographics,  and  spousal  characteristics  in  
17:580:33605:28:27:90:530:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1992.      The   survey   also   asked   detailed   questions   about   household   income,   tax   
17:581:33705:27:28:90:527:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:information,  and  IRA  contributions,  but,  as  is  true  in  many  household  surveys,  these  
17:582:33803:28:28:90:524:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:questions were for the previous calendar year, 1991.  So, for the purposes of the empirical 
17:583:33895:28:27:90:414:294:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:analysis, periods t and 1+t refer to 1991 and 1992, respectively.   
17:584:33963:27:28:125:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Questions on employment were asked for the job (if any) held at the time of the 
17:585:34043:28:28:90:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:interview, as well as previous jobs.  A unique feature of these data is that the HRS used 
17:586:34133:28:27:90:525:211:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  job  rosters  from  the  household  interviews  and  collected  Summary  Plan  Descriptions  
17:587:34231:27:28:90:524:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(SPDs), which are legal descriptions of pensions written in plain English, from employers 
17:588:34321:28:27:90:527:156:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of  HRS  respondents  for  all  current  and  previous  jobs  in  which  the  respondent  was  
17:589:34416:27:20:90:529:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:covered   by   a   pension.      These   descriptions   help   to   sidestep   the   problems   with   
17:590:34519:20:8:90:237:109:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
17:591:34567:8:16:90:526:101:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:5  See  Mitchell  (1988),  Starr-McCluer  and  Sunden  (1999),  Johnson,  Sambamoorthi,  and  Crystal  (2000),  
17:592:34679:16:11:90:527:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Gustman  and  Steinmeier  (1999),  Rohwedder  (2003a,  2003b),  and  Engelhardt  (2001)  for  evidence  on  
17:593:34787:11:0:90:239:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:measurement error in pension data.   
18:594:34825:0:27:90:530:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:measurement   error   outlined   above,   and,   instead,   measure   the   exact   incentives   to   
18:595:34927:27:28:90:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contribute by using the employer matching formulas given in the SPD.6   Specifically, the 
18:596:35017:28:27:89:528:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:job  in  which  the  respondent  was  employed  in  1991  was  identified  and  then  SPDs  
18:597:35109:27:28:89:525:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:associated with that job that had dates of adoption after 1991 were excluded.  In addition, 
18:598:35201:28:28:89:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the date of last amendment and dates for changes in plan provisions indicated in the text 
18:599:35291:28:27:89:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of the SPD were used to exclude plans that were in existence in 1991 but whose features 
18:600:35379:27:28:89:390:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:changed between 1991 and the time the SPD was collected.     
18:601:35440:28:27:125:526:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The  HRS  also  asked  in  the  first  wave  the  respondents’  permission  to  link  their  
18:602:35533:27:28:90:530:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:survey   responses   to   administrative   earnings   data   from   SSA   and   IRS.      These   
18:603:35631:28:28:90:527:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:administrative  data  include  Social  Security  covered-earnings  histories  from  1951-1991  
18:604:35726:28:27:90:524:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and W-2 earnings records for jobs held from 1980-1991, and were made available for use 
18:605:35813:27:28:90:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:under a restricted-access confidential data agreement.  They are the basis for two critical 
18:606:35905:28:27:90:527:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:measures  in  the  analysis  dataset.    First,  the  W-2  data  provide  administrative  data  on  
18:607:36005:27:28:90:528:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:earnings  and  401(k)  contributions  for  1991.    Unlike  the  contributions  data  used  in  
18:608:36101:28:27:90:529:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:previous  studies,  these  data  are  not  subject  to  measurement  error,  as  they  are  the  
18:609:36198:27:28:90:528:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer’s  official  report  to  the  government  on  annual  earnings  and  elective  deferrals.    
18:610:36300:28:28:90:527:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Second,  when  combined,  the  W-2  earnings  histories,  Social  Security  covered-earnings  
18:611:36394:28:27:90:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:histories  and  self-reported  earnings  histories,  allowed  for  the  construction  of  complete  
18:612:36494:27:28:90:526:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:earnings  histories  from  1951-1991  for  each  member  of  our  sample.    When  used  with  
18:613:36589:28:27:90:528:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Social  Security  and  pension-benefit  calculators,  which  are  described  in  Appendix  B,  
18:614:36684:27:28:90:526:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:these  data  allowed  for  the  calculation  of  the  public  and  private  pension  wealth,  accruals  
18:615:36788:28:32:90:374:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and changes in accruals, for 1991 and 1992, respectively.   
18:616:36848:32:7:90:237:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
18:617:36896:7:16:90:526:90:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:6  The  data  appendix  explains  why  self-reported  pension  information  was  not  used  and  some  other  data  
18:618:37012:16:0:90:187:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:limitations in the HRS.  
19:619:37039:0:27:125:527:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Overall,  when  all  of  the  sources  are  combined,  the  data  are  a  comprehensive  
19:620:37128:27:28:90:526:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:description  of  the  household’s  financial  situation  and  exact  pension  incentives  in  1991  
19:621:37228:28:27:90:524:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and 1992 with which to estimate the parameters in the empirical specification in (15) and 
19:622:37318:27:28:90:524:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:a significantly richer data source than previous studies.   Specifically, the sample consists 
19:623:37412:28:28:90:427:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of 1,042 HRS individuals eligible to contribute to a 401(k) in 1991.     
19:624:37484:28:27:90:93:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
19:625:37484:27:28:90:218:543:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:VI. Descriptive Statistics 
19:626:37510:28:27:126:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Many plans limit the amount of the match.  These caps are usually expressed as a 
19:627:37591:27:28:89:521:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent of pay in the SPD, but also can be a percent of contributions, and even a fixed-
19:628:37679:28:28:89:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:dollar  amount.    Table  1  shows  the  distribution  of  matching  caps  in  the  analysis  sample,  
19:629:37782:28:27:89:527:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:expressed  as  a  percent  of  annual  pay.    About  19  percent  of  these  plans  had  caps  on  
19:630:37882:27:28:89:527:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer  matching  that  were  less  than  four  percent  of  pay.    The  median  cap  was  6  
19:631:37979:28:27:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent of pay, but 15 percent of plans had higher caps.  Plans also vary according to the 
19:632:38070:27:28:89:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:match  rate.  Table  2  shows  the  distribution  of  “first-dollar”  match  rates  in  the  analysis  
19:633:38173:28:27:89:526:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sample.    Columns  1  and  2  indicate  that  these  match  rates  were  clustered  at  25,  50,  and  
19:634:38277:27:28:89:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:100  percent,  where  the  median  match  rate  was  50  percent.    However,  27  percent  of  the  
19:635:38378:28:28:89:526:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:plans offered matches of 100 percent, and three plans offered match rates of 200 percent.   
19:636:38470:28:27:125:527:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Descriptive  statistics  for  selected  variables  used  in  the  empirical  analysis  are  
19:637:38562:27:28:90:525:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:shown in Table 3.  Column 1 shows sample means for the full sample, with the standard 
19:638:38648:28:27:89:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:deviation in parentheses, and the median in square brackets.  Overall, the sample consists 
19:639:38739:27:28:89:526:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of  mostly  white,  married  individuals  in  their  mid-50s,  with  some  college  education  and  
19:640:38839:28:28:89:526:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:relatively  few  children  at  home.    Only  56.4  percent  of  the  sample  actively  participated  
19:641:38941:28:0:90:527:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(defined  as  having  made  a  positive  contribution)  in  1991.      The  sample  mean  401(k)  
20:642:39041:0:27:90:528:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contribution  in  calendar  year  1991  was  $1,377,  but  among  contributors,  the  average  
20:643:39136:27:28:90:526:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contribution  was  $2,446  (shown  in  column  4).    Only  3  percent  of  the  sample  made  the  
20:644:39236:28:27:89:211:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:maximum contribution.   
20:645:39260:27:28:126:528:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Figure  1  plots  the  distribution  of  401(k)  contributions  for  the  match-eligible  
20:646:39350:28:28:90:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:individuals in the sample in intervals of $200 relative to the kink amount.  As illustrated 
20:647:39442:28:27:90:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in  the  figure,  there  is  substantial  bunching  of  contributions  at  the  kink  (measured  as  the  
20:648:39548:27:28:90:525:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:value 0 on the horizontal axis).  About 25 percent of match-eligible individuals locate at 
20:649:39639:28:27:90:324:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:or within $400 of the kink on their budget sets.   
20:650:39690:27:28:126:530:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:A   comparison   of   contributions   between   those   without   and   with   employer   
20:651:39780:28:28:90:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:matching  in  columns  2  and  3  of  Table  3,  respectively,  indicates  that  individuals  with  
20:652:39880:28:27:89:525:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:matching contributed just over $400 more on average than those without matching (i.e., 
20:653:39967:27:28:89:526:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:$1,640-$1,232=$408).    The  difference  in  the  median  contributions  between  these  two  
20:654:40061:28:27:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:groups was $800.    Therefore, just based on a comparison of means, it would appear that 
20:655:40150:27:28:89:355:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:there is a small response of 401(k) saving to matching. 
20:656:40206:28:27:126:527:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:A  comparison  of  columns  2  and  3  in  Table  3  also  indicates  that  plans  with  
20:657:40295:27:28:89:526:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer  matching  differ  along  other  dimensions  that  may  make  saving  attractive.    For  
20:658:40394:28:28:89:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:example, if there is an employer match, the individual is much more likely to be able to 
20:659:40483:28:27:89:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:borrow  against  the  plan  balance,  direct  the  investment  of  plan  balances,  less  likely  to  
20:660:40585:27:28:89:526:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have  another  traditional  pension  plan,  more  likely  to  have  the  plan  annual  contribution  
20:661:40686:28:27:89:527:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:limit  lower  than  the  federal  limit,  and  more  likely  to  be  allowed  to  make  after-tax  
20:662:40785:27:28:89:212:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contributions to the plan. 
20:663:40812:28:28:126:129:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
20:664:40812:28:0:90:413:101:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:VII.   Explaining Unused Employer Matching Contributions 
21:665:40870:0:27:125:528:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Because  the  typical  employer  match  yields  a  return  far  exceeding  that  on  
21:666:40955:27:28:89:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:alternative  investments,  401(k)  participation  would  be  predicted  to  be  100  percent  if  all  
21:667:41058:28:27:89:528:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:individuals  were  fully  informed,  financially  rational,  with  access  to  perfect  capital  
21:668:41155:27:28:89:525:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:markets  and  no  transactions  costs.    In  addition,  at  a  minimum,  all  participants  would  be  
21:669:41259:28:28:89:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:predicted  to  maximize  total  compensation  and  contribute  up  to  the  point  at  which  the  
21:670:41358:28:27:89:528:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer  match  was  exhausted  and  then  engage  in  a  set  of  borrowing  and  lending  
21:671:41451:27:28:89:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:arrangements to achieve the desired level of consumption and leisure.7   Yet in Table 3, 
21:672:41540:28:27:89:526:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:401(k)  participation  is  56.4  percent  among  all  sample  individuals,  and  only  54  percent  
21:673:41640:27:28:89:524:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:among those offered a match.  This suggests that individuals left “money on the table” by 
21:674:41730:28:28:89:326:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:not capturing the total potential employer match. 
21:675:41780:28:27:125:525:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Column 1 of Table 4 shows the total potential employer match in the sample for 
21:676:41859:27:28:89:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:individuals eligible for a match.  The mean potential match was $1,249, or 3.8 percent of 
21:677:41949:28:27:89:526:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:annual  pay.    The  average  employer  match  that  went  unused  because  contributions  were  
21:678:42046:27:28:89:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:not  made  up  to  the  level  of  the  match  cap  was  $550,  or  1.9  percent  of  pay.    Naturally,  
21:679:42152:28:27:89:524:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:non-participants accounted for most of this, with the unused match equal to 3.7 percent of 
21:680:42243:27:28:89:527:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:pay  (column  3).    Even  more  striking,  though,  is  that  among  participants  the  average  
21:681:42341:28:28:89:413:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:unused employer match represented 1 percent of pay (column 2).8

25:802:51734:16:11:89:524:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:including the vector z in x.  We could not reject the null hypothesis that these additional variables jointly

26:809:52319:27:28:89:527:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:      A  final  issue  is  that  the  sample  is  likely  non-random  because  it  is  based  on  
26:810:52417:28:28:89:527:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:individuals  for  whom  the  HRS  was  able  to  obtain  an  employer-provided  SPD  for  the  
26:811:52512:28:27:89:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:401(k) plan.  Although previous pension studies using the HRS employer-provided SPDs 
26:812:52597:27:28:89:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have  not  corrected  for  selection  because  of  the  lack  of  plausible  exclusion  restrictions,  
26:813:52700:28:27:89:524:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:two exclusion restrictions based on IRS Form 5500 data were used to estimate the model 
26:814:52787:27:28:89:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:using a number of methods to correct for selection.  The first exclusion is the incidence of 
26:815:52880:28:28:89:527:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:pension-plan  outsourcing  by  Census  region,  employment-size  category,  one-digit  SIC  
26:816:52972:28:27:89:526:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:code,  and  union  status  (union  plan  vs.  non-union  plan)  cell  in  1992,  where  outsourcing  
26:817:53073:27:28:89:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:means  the  plan  was  administered  by  an  entity  other  than  the  employer.    The  intuition  is  
26:818:53177:28:27:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that the HRS is less likely to obtain an SPD from the employer if (on average in its cell) 
26:819:53268:27:28:89:527:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:plan  administration  is  outsourced,  because  more  than  one  contact  is  needed  (first  the  
26:820:53367:28:27:89:525:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer,  then  the  plan  administrator)  to  receive  the  SPD.    The  second  exclusion  is  the  
26:821:53470:27:28:89:527:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:incidence  of  pension-plan  consolidation  due  to  mergers  and  acquisitions  by  cell  from  
26:822:53567:28:28:89:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1988-1992.  The intuition is that the HRS is less likely either to obtain an SPD from the 
26:823:53657:28:27:89:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer  or  match  it  to  the  employee  if  (on  average  in  its  cell)  there  has  been  a  lot  of  
26:824:53765:27:28:89:528:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:plan consolidation, because plan names and detail are often changed upon consolidation.  
26:825:53854:28:27:89:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Finally, two other variables based on HRS data were used as exclusions in the selection 
26:826:53942:27:28:89:525:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:equations: dummies for whether the individual left the job because the business closed or 
26:827:54032:28:28:89:526:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:was laid off, respectively.  These help to measure whether the employer possibly was in 
26:828:54120:28:0:89:525:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:financial difficulty at severance, which, if that resulted in a business failure, would have 
27:829:54215:0:27:90:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:made  it  more  difficult  for  the  HRS  to  have  obtained  an  SPD.    The  construction  of  the  
27:830:54317:27:28:89:456:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:exclusions and the selection equation are discussed in detail in Appendix B. 
27:831:54394:28:27:89:92:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
27:832:54394:27:28:90:213:626:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:X.  Estimation Results

27:834:54511:30:30:89:524:568:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:vector x in is limited to a constant, by maximum likelihood, where ),0(~2σNu.  Panel

27:837:54786:27:28:89:526:483:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:parameter  estimates  for  the  baseline  specification  without  instrumenting.    The  marginal  
27:838:54885:28:28:89:526:455:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:effect  for  a  one  unit  change  in  the  match  rate  represents  an  increase  of  one  dollar  of  
27:839:54989:28:27:89:528:427:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:match  per  dollar  of  employee  contribution  and  is  shown  in  Panel.13    The  estimated  
27:840:55085:27:28:90:528:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:marginal  effect  of  an  increase  in  the  match  rate  by  one  dollar  is  an  increase  in

27:842:55278:27:28:90:526:345:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:extremely  small  and  statistically  different  than  zero,  based  on  the  p-value  for  the  test  of  
27:843:55385:28:28:90:525:317:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the null hypothesis of no impact of employer matching shown in panel A.  The estimated

27:846:55671:28:27:90:385:234:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:economic magnitude of the income elasticity is very small.    
27:847:55733:27:28:126:525:207:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Column 2 gives the instrumental-variable estimates.  In panel B, an increase in the

27:849:55907:28:27:90:527:151:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is  statistically  different  than  zero.    This  estimate  is  substantially  larger  than  the  one  in  
27:850:56015:27:15:90:528:124:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:column  1  without  instrumenting,  which  indicates  substantial  downward  bias  in  the  
27:851:56107:15:8:90:237:109:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:

27:853:56272:16:7:89:185:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:instrumental variables.  
27:854:56297:7:0:90:445:78:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:13 The 95% bias-corrected bootstrapped confidence interval is shown in square brackets. 
28:855:56387:0:27:90:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:estimated match effect from endogeneity.   In column 2, the income effect is negative and 
28:856:56477:27:28:90:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:indicates that an increase of one unit in virtual full income, which represents an increase 
28:857:56569:28:27:90:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of $100,000, results in an estimated reduction in the probability of participation of eight 
28:858:56661:27:28:89:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percentage  points.    The  income  effect,  as  well  as  the  impact  of  the  net  wage  and  the  
28:859:56763:28:28:89:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:marginal tax rate, are all significant at less than the 0.0001 level of significance for all of 
28:860:56859:28:27:89:236:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the specifications in Table 7.   
28:861:56892:27:28:126:525:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:To get a better sense of the economic magnitude of these marginal effects, Panel 
28:862:56973:28:27:90:524:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:D shows the estimated elasticity of participation with respect to the employer match rate, 
28:863:57064:27:28:90:527:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:evaluated  at  the  sample  means.    In  column  2,  the  estimated  elasticity  is  0.07:  if  the  
28:864:57166:28:28:90:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer  match  were  raised  from  twenty-five  to  fifty  cents  (i.e.,  doubled),  participation  
28:865:57268:28:27:90:528:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:would  rise  by  seven  percent  (not  percentage  points).14      Thus,  401(k)  participation  
28:866:57365:27:28:89:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:appears to be quite inelastic with respect to the employer match.  The estimated income 
28:867:57453:28:28:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:elasticity is -0.10; the estimated net wage elasticity is 04.0−; and the estimated elasticity 
28:868:57547:28:27:89:526:349:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:with  respect  to  the  marginal  tax  rate  is  0.04,  so  that  401(k)  participation  also  is  very  
28:869:57652:27:28:89:280:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:inelastic with respect to the tax price.    
28:870:57696:28:27:126:526:294:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Panel  A  also  shows  the  parameter  estimates  on  the  exclusion  restrictions  in  the  
28:871:57789:27:28:89:527:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:selection  model.15  The p-value  for  the  test  of  the  null  hypothesis  that  the  exclusions  
28:872:57889:28:28:90:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:jointly do not explain who has a matched SPD, though not shown in the table, is less than 
28:873:57979:28:27:90:525:211:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:0.01, which indicates the exclusions have predictive power for who is in the sample.  In 
28:874:58068:27:28:90:531:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:particular,   greater   plan   outsourcing,   consolidation,   business   closure   and   layoffs   
28:875:58168:28:27:90:525:156:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:significantly decrease the likelihood  of  having  a  matched  SPD.    The  parameter  estimate  
28:876:58265:27:32:90:528:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:on  the  selection  term  in  the  participation  equation  is  negative,  and,  based  on  the  
28:877:58362:32:7:90:237:97:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
28:878:58410:7:12:90:434:90:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:14 The estimated elasticities are very similar when based on individual characteristics. 
28:879:58499:12:0:90:404:78:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:15  Parameter estimates for the full selection model are available upon request. 
29:880:58582:0:27:90:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:associated standard error, the null hypothesis of no selection bias can be rejected at the 3 
29:881:58675:27:28:90:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:percent level of significance.  This is evidence of selection: high savers are less likely to 
29:882:58769:28:27:90:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have  an  employer-provided  SPD  in  the  HRS,  consistent  with  the  reduced-form  analysis  
29:883:58865:27:28:90:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of  Gustman  and  Steinmeier  (1999).    To  gauge  whether  this  selection  is  economically  
29:884:58961:28:28:90:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:important,  column  3  shows  the  IV  results  without  selection  correction.    The  estimated  
29:885:59060:28:27:90:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participation  elasticity  with  respect  to  the  match  rate  in  Panel  E  is  now  0.19,  which  is  
29:886:59165:27:28:90:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:more  than  double  the  selection-corrected  elasticity  of  0.07  in  column  2.    This  indicates  
29:887:59268:28:27:90:527:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:that  the  bias  from  estimating  the  determinants  of  401(k)  participation  on  the  selected  
29:888:59368:27:28:89:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sample of the respondents in the HRS who have matched SPDs has a substantial effect on 
29:889:59455:28:28:89:378:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the economic magnitude of the employer match estimates.   
29:890:59513:28:27:125:128:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
29:891:59513:27:28:89:260:405:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f6:C:Robustness Checks and Extensions 
29:892:59546:28:27:125:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:There are two practical concerns in the estimation that fall outside of the scope of 
29:893:59631:27:28:89:525:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  theoretical  framework.    First,  firms  may  offer  employer  matching  contributions  as  a  
29:894:59732:28:27:89:526:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:way  to  try  to  avoid  failing  federal  pension  non-discrimination  rules  because  they  have  
29:895:59832:27:28:89:526:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:low-saving  employees  (McGill,  et  al.,  1996).  This  would  tend  to  bias  downward  the  
29:896:59927:28:28:89:526:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:estimated  match  elasticity.    Second,  firms  that  match  may  adopt  other  plan  features  to  
29:897:60028:28:27:89:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:stimulate employee saving (e.g., allow for borrowing against plan balances, self-directed 
29:898:60118:27:28:89:529:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:investment,  offer  after-tax  saving  options,  offer  retirement  seminars,  etc.)  or  offer  
29:899:60215:28:27:89:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:different fringe benefit packages that might affect saving behavior than firms that do not 
29:900:60306:27:28:89:436:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:match.  This would tend to bias upward the estimated match elasticity.   
29:901:60379:28:28:125:526:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The  reduced-form  relationship  between  employer  match  rates  and  these  factors  
29:902:60466:28:0:89:527:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:using the HRS data was examined in a companion paper, Engelhardt and Kumar (2004a).  
30:903:60553:0:27:90:527:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:As  described  there,  the  non-discrimination  rules  are  set  up  so  that  employers  with  a  
30:904:60652:27:28:90:522:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:greater  proportion  of  workers  with  earnings  large  enough  to  be  deemed  “highly-
30:905:60741:28:27:90:522:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compensated   employees”   under   federal   law   face   greater   pressure   to   meet   non-
30:906:60836:27:28:90:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:discrimination  rules  if  they  offer  a  401(k).    In  particular,  a  variable  that  measured  the  
30:907:60941:28:28:89:521:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:share of workers with earnings above the federal threshold for the definition of a “highly-
30:908:61032:28:27:90:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compensated” employee under federal non-discrimination regulations in the respondent’s 
30:909:61119:27:28:90:528:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Census-region-by-employment-size-category-by-one-digit-SIC-code-by-union-status  cell  
30:910:61206:28:27:90:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in  1989  was  constructed  from  the  March  CPS.    This  measure  was  then  weighted  by  the  
30:911:61305:27:28:90:526:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:difference  in  combined  federal  and  state  marginal  tax  rates  on  earnings  for  the  median  
30:912:61406:28:28:90:522:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:highly-  and  non-highly-compensated  workers  in  the  cell  to  reflect  the  value  a  highly-
30:913:61503:28:27:89:527:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:compensated  worker  would  put  on  a  dollar  of  tax-deferred  salary  through  a  401(k)  
30:914:61597:27:28:89:525:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:relative to that for a non-highly-compensated worker.  This tax-difference-weighted share 
30:915:61687:28:27:90:529:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:was  used  as  a  measure  of  the  non-discrimination  “pressure”  faced  by  the  typical  
30:916:61780:27:28:90:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer in the respondent’s cell in a reduced-form model of the determinants of match 
30:917:61867:28:27:90:201:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rates in the HRS data.  
30:918:61891:27:28:126:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The estimation results in Engelhardt and Kumar (2004a) showed that the measure 
30:919:61970:28:28:90:527:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of  pressure  and  other  plan  characteristics  were  highly  significant.    For  example,  the  
30:920:62069:28:27:90:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:greater the pressure (tax-difference-weighted share) the more likely the respondent’s plan 
30:921:62160:27:28:90:522:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:offered a match and the higher the match rate.  Also, plans that allowed borrowing, self-
30:922:62249:28:27:90:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:directed  investment,  had  other  traditional  features,  had  limits  less  than  the  federal  limit,  
30:923:62355:27:0:90:525:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and after-tax saving options had significantly higher first-dollar employer match rates, as 
31:924:62449:0:27:90:527:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:was  suggested  in  the  comparison  of  unconditional  means  in  Table  3  of  the  current  
31:925:62544:27:28:90:137:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:paper.16   
31:926:62555:28:27:125:525:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:With  this  in  mind,  two  groups  of  additional  explanatory  variables  were  included  
31:927:62647:27:28:89:524:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in the vector x in (15) for the specification in Table 7: 1) fringe benefits offered: dummy 
31:928:62739:28:28:89:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:variables for whether the firm offered long-term disability and group term life insurance, 
31:929:62830:28:27:89:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:respectively,  as  well  as  the  number  of  health  insurance  plans,  number  of  retiree  health  
31:930:62932:27:28:89:524:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:insurance plans, weeks paid vacation, and days of sick pay; 2) other plan characteristics: 
31:931:63023:28:27:90:521:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:dummy variables for whether the 401(k) allowed borrowing, hardship withdrawals, self-

34:1052:71495:11:12:90:527:189:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:The  CLAD  point  estimates  produced  marginal  effects  that  were  very  similar  to  the  SCLS  and  Tobit
