34:1054:71721:11:12:90:525:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:estimator frequently failed to converge.  In particular, as is well-known for LAD estimators, the estimator 
34:1055:71829:12:11:90:525:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:can  fail  to  converge  when  the  specification  becomes  more  and  more  saturated  with  control  variables  and  
34:1056:71948:11:12:90:527:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:the  cells  become  thin,  as  in  the  richer  specifications  in  subsequent  columns  in  Table  8.    This  is  a  
34:1057:72067:12:11:90:526:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:particularly  severe  problem  for  CLAD  estimators  that  rely  on  iterative  trimming  of  the  data  when  the  
34:1058:72184:11:12:90:526:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:analysis  dataset  is  not  large,  because  the  estimation  dataset  becomes  smaller  with  each  iteration,  even  
34:1059:72303:12:11:90:525:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:though the number of explanatory variables remains the same.  In this application, the estimation algorithm 
34:1060:72411:11:12:90:524:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:trimmed the original 1,042 observations down to around 400 by the last iteration.  For this reason, reliable 
34:1061:72520:12:11:90:525:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:bootstrapped  standard  errors  were  not  able  to  be  obtained  for  CLAD  estimates  and  they  are  not  shown  in  
34:1062:72641:11:0:90:133:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Table 8.    
35:1063:72655:0:27:90:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participation model in Table 7.  Finally, Based on a Hausman-type test (Newey, 1987a), 
35:1064:72742:27:28:89:469:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:we could not reject the IV Tobit model in favor of the IV SCLS specification.  
35:1065:72821:28:27:126:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Table  10  shows  the  estimated  marginal  effect  and  elasticities  for  the  employer  
35:1066:72912:27:28:89:525:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:match rate by sex and education group for the richest specification, shown in column 10 
35:1067:73000:28:28:89:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:of  Table  9.  In  columns  1  and  2  of  Table  10,  an  increase  in  the  match  rate  of  one  dollar  
35:1068:73108:28:27:89:528:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increases  contributions  of  females  and  males  by  an  estimated  $1,153  and  $1,752,  
35:1069:73200:27:28:89:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:respectively.    The  results  for  the  education  groups  echo  those  from  the  discrete  choice  
35:1070:73302:28:27:89:526:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:model of participation in Table 8, both marginal effects and elasticities rise sharply with 
35:1071:73394:27:28:89:148:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:education.   
35:1072:73407:28:28:89:92:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
35:1073:73407:28:27:90:254:432:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:XI. Summary and Implications  
35:1074:73436:27:28:126:527:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Previous  studies  have  produced  a  puzzling  array  of  estimates  of  the  impact  of  
35:1075:73527:28:27:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer matching on 401(k) saving.  This probably stemmed from the use of less than 
35:1076:73612:27:28:89:525:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:ideal data and, more importantly, the failure to incorporate into estimation match-induced 
35:1077:73703:28:27:89:527:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:kinks  in  the  budget  set.    Overall  in  this  analysis,  based  on  the  life-cycle  consistent  
35:1078:73805:27:28:89:526:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:specification  derived,  the  estimated  elasticity  of  401(k)  participation  with  respect  to  the  
35:1079:73909:28:28:89:528:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:match  rate  ranged  from  0.02-0.07,  and,  hence,  participation  was  quite  inelastic  with  
35:1080:74006:28:27:89:524:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:respect to employer matching, a pattern that was apparent even in a simple comparison of 
35:1081:74095:27:28:89:527:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:means.  The  estimated  elasticities  of  401(k)  saving  from  a  censored  regression  model  
35:1082:74191:28:27:89:498:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:ranged from 0.09-0.12 with just under half of this response on the intensive margin.  
35:1083:74277:27:28:125:525:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:There are two obvious limitations of these findings.  First, the focus was on older 
35:1084:74361:28:28:89:525:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:workers,  for  whom  the  very  detailed  data  for  this  type  of  study  were  available;  whether  
35:1085:74464:28:0:89:527:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  estimates  apply  to  younger  workers  is  an  open  question.    Second,  this  study  has  
36:1086:74565:0:27:90:524:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:nothing to say about the broader question of to what extent 401(k) saving constitutes new 
36:1087:74655:27:28:90:384:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:private saving, a point of substantial debate in the literature.  
36:1088:74721:28:27:90:529:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:  Given  these  caveats,  there  are  a  number  of  potential  implications  of  these  
36:1089:74810:27:28:90:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:findings.  First, because of the estimated inelastic response on both the intensive and the 
36:1090:74902:28:28:90:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:extensive margins, the analysis reveals that for employers and policy makers interested in 
36:1091:74993:28:27:90:526:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:promoting  retirement  saving  by  older  workers  through  greater  401(k)  participation  and  
36:1092:75090:27:28:89:526:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:saving,  matching  is  a  rather  poor  policy  instrument.    Roughly  speaking,  the  estimated  
36:1093:75189:28:27:89:526:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:marginal  effects  in  this  paper  suggest  that  an  increase  in  the  employer  match  rate  of  $1  
36:1094:75294:27:28:89:528:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:per  $1  of  employee  contribution  would  be  needed  to  achieve  the  same  increase  in  
36:1095:75388:28:28:89:526:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:participation  as  the  implementation  of  automatic  enrollment,  based  on  the  estimates  in  
36:1096:75487:28:27:89:534:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Madrian  and  Shea  (2001)  and  Choi,  Laibson,  Madrian,  and  Metrick  (2002,  2004).      
36:1097:75581:27:28:89:529:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Automatic  enrollment  would  seem  to  be  a  much  more  effective  way  to  increase  
36:1098:75670:28:27:89:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:retirement saving.  Second, a number of commonly-advocated reforms to Social Security 
36:1099:75756:27:28:89:525:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:call for the introduction of voluntary private accounts, to which individuals could choose 
36:1100:75847:28:27:90:525:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to contribute additional funds toward Social Security.  Under some proposals, the federal 
36:1101:75937:27:28:90:528:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:government  would  match  those  contributions  as  an  incentive.    In  designing  such  a  
36:1102:76031:28:28:90:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:system, it would be instrumental for policy makers to know how individual contributions 
36:1103:76119:28:27:90:528:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:would  respond  to  the  government  match.    Our  analysis  suggests  that  government  
36:1104:76209:27:28:90:528:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:matching  of  voluntary  contributions  to  any  type  of  Social  Security  personal  account  
36:1105:76305:28:27:89:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:would  be  relatively  ineffective  in  promoting  personal-account  contributions  (Engelhardt  
36:1106:76402:27:28:89:525:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and  Kumar,  2005).    Third,  beyond  personal  accounts,  there  is  substantial  policy  interest  
36:1107:76504:28:28:89:527:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in  the  government  provision  of  matching  contributions  designed  to  stimulate  targeted  
36:1108:76600:28:0:89:525:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:forms of saving among lower income households, which has led researchers to evaluate 
37:1109:76687:0:27:90:528:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  impact  of  Individual  Development  Accounts  (IDA)  [Mills,  Gale,  Patterson,  and  
37:1110:76779:27:28:90:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Apostolov, 2006], federal programs for matching IRA contributions, and the adoption of 
37:1111:76866:28:27:89:526:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  Saver’s  Credit  [Duflo,  Gale,  Liebman,  Orszag,  and  Saez,  2006].    In  particular,  the  
37:1112:76967:27:28:89:529:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Mills,   et   al.   and   Duflo,   et   al.   analyses,   which   were   based   on   randomized   field   
37:1113:77074:28:28:89:532:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:experiments,    have    shown    substantially    more    elastic    responses    from    matching    
37:1114:77176:28:27:90:378:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contributions on IDA and IRA contributions, respectively.   
37:1115:77236:27:28:126:528:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Our  reading  of  these  two  studies  suggests  that  their  findings  are  difficult  to  
37:1116:77328:28:27:90:528:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:extrapolate  to  employer  matching  contributions  in  corporate  401(k)  plans  for  three  
37:1117:77422:27:28:90:528:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:reasons.    First,  eligible  employees  in  401(k)  plans  are  not  typically  lower  income  
37:1118:77518:28:28:90:527:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:individuals.    They  are  more  likely  to  be  substantially  better  off  economically.    For  
37:1119:77617:28:27:90:526:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:example,  individuals  in  the  Mills  et  al.  analysis  had  incomes  below  150  percent  of  the  
37:1120:77719:27:28:90:531:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:poverty   line.      Second,   institutional   features   differ   substantially.      For   example,   
37:1121:77823:28:27:90:527:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contributions  to  a  401(k)  plan  that  are  matched  are  typically  done  through  automatic  
37:1122:77921:27:28:90:524:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:payroll deduction, whereas contributions to IDAs and IRAs in the Mills, et al. and Duflo, 
37:1123:78011:28:27:90:526:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:et  al.  analyses  were  not.    Third,  the  matching  contributions  in  the  Duflo,  et  al.  analysis  
37:1124:78118:27:28:90:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:were offered as part of an unannounced, take-it-or-leave-it decision, whereas employees 
37:1125:78206:28:28:90:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in a 401(k) can respond to a match by contributing at any point in a given calendar year, 
37:1126:78296:28:27:90:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:or  even  a  different  calendar  year,  without  foregoing  the  option  of  being  eligible  for  a  
37:1127:78399:27:28:90:529:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:match.      Overall,   although   these   are   fascinating   studies   that   will   have   important   
37:1128:78504:28:27:90:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:implications for policy targeted to lower income households and, through randomization, 
37:1129:78592:27:28:90:526:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have  convincingly  addressed  important  issues  in  the  econometric  identification  of  the  
37:1130:78689:28:28:90:528:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:causal  effects  of  matching,  these  studies  are  of  limited  use  in  formulating  policy  
37:1131:78785:28:0:90:219:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:concerning 401(k) plans.   
38:1132:78814:0:28:125:525:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Finally,  a  number  of  prominent  companies  have  reduced  or  eliminated  matching  
38:1133:78902:28:30:89:524:680:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contributions recently due to declining profits.Although it remains to be seen if this is a 
38:1134:78994:30:28:89:526:650:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:long-term  trend,  understanding  the  impact  of  matching  is  critical  to  understanding  the  
38:1135:79093:28:27:89:527:622:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:impact  of  these  changes  on  retirement  income  security  for  a  workforce  increasingly  
38:1136:79188:27:28:89:527:595:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:dependent  on  401(k)  plans  for  retirement.    The  fact  that  the  estimated  response  of  
38:1137:79285:28:27:89:524:567:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contributions to the employer match in this paper was quite inelastic suggests that overall 
38:1138:79377:27:28:89:526:540:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:401(k) activity at these firms might not be greatly affected by these changes in matching.   
38:1139:79470:28:0:125:128:512:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:

48:1516:98717:0:13:273:341:708:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C: Appendix A

48:1518:98729:14:14:126:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:This appendix lays out the theoretical model in more detail.  Additional detail can 
48:1519:98813:14:14:89:525:667:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:be  provided  upon  request.    This  appendix  is  intended  to  be  supplemental  and,  given  its  
48:1520:98915:14:14:89:196:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:length, not published. 
48:1521:98938:14:13:126:129:639:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
48:1522:98938:13:14:126:528:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Previous  studies  have  had  two  important  shortcomings.    First,  they  have  not  
48:1523:99026:14:14:89:526:612:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:couched  their  analyses  in  formal  models  of  intertemporal  choice,  even  though  saving  
48:1524:99122:14:14:89:526:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:involves  the  substitution  of  resources  across  time.    This  means  that  previous  estimates  
48:1525:99223:14:14:89:525:584:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:cannot  be  interpreted  as  estimates  of  life-cycle-consistent  determinants  of  401(k)  saving  
48:1526:99324:14:13:89:528:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:necessarily,  because  the  empirical  specifications  may  not  have  been  consistent  with  
48:1527:99419:13:14:89:527:557:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:underlying  utility  maximization.    So,  while  the  existing  literature  has  provided  quite  
48:1528:99518:14:14:89:525:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:informative descriptive analyses, it has said little about how 401(k) saving may respond 
48:1529:99607:14:14:89:524:529:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to prospective changes in employer matching or what the optimal match rate should be to 
48:1530:99695:14:14:89:527:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:achieve  a  saving  target.  Second,  with  the  exception  of  Choi,  Laibson,  Madrian,  and  
48:1531:99791:14:13:90:527:501:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Metrick  (2002)  and  VanDerhei  and  Copeland  (2001),  previous  studies  have  failed  to  
48:1532:99885:13:14:90:525:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:exploit the fact that multiple-match-rate schedules and caps on matching induce kinks in 
48:1533:99974:14:14:90:180:474:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the budget set.20    
48:1534:99995:14:14:126:129:460:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C: 
48:1535:99995:14:14:126:526:446:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:To illustrate the kink, Figure 1 shows budget sets with and without matching in a 
48:1536:100077:14:14:89:530:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:simple   two-period   model   of   consumption   (without   borrowing)   typically   used   in   
48:1537:100174:14:18:89:525:418:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:undergraduate textbooks.  Let 1C and 2C be consumption in period 1 when working and 
48:1538:100258:18:18:89:527:400:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:period  2  when  retired,  respectively,  and  ly1  be  first-period  gross  labor  earnings.    For  
48:1539:100360:18:18:89:526:382:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:simplicity, assume federal marginal income tax rates, F1θ, in the first period, and F2θ, in 
48:1540:100452:18:14:89:526:364:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  second  period,  and  no  labor  earnings  in  the  second  period.    Let  SSW  be  the  present  
48:1541:100556:14:14:90:525:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:value of traditional Social Security wealth, r be the gross return, and assume that Social 
48:1542:100647:14:17:89:525:336:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Security is not taxed when retired.  Assume that the 401(k) is the only form of voluntary 
48:1543:100737:17:19:89:525:319:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:saving, and contributions, VOLQ, measured in dollars from right to left on the horizontal 
48:1544:100827:19:18:89:526:300:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:axis, are matched at a fixed rate, VOLm,  up  to  a  cap,  matchQ, based on the amount of the 
48:1545:100921:18:19:90:524:282:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:voluntary contributions.  The upper limit on voluntary contributions is maxQ.  The budget 
48:1546:101011:19:16:90:524:263:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:constraint without matching is abcd.  With matching, it is abkhi, and from 0 to matchQ 
48:1547:101097:16:23:89:541:247:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(reading      right      to      left,      beginning      at      point      a),      the      slope      is      
48:1548:101212:23:8:90:237:224:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:                                                 
48:1549:101260:8:16:90:527:216:42:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:20  Both  of  these  studies  examined  the  impact  of  match  rates  and  caps  on  401(k)  participation  and  
48:1550:101374:16:11:89:526:200:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:contributions,  but  from  rather  different  perspectives  than  in  this  paper.    Specifically,  Choi,  Laibson,  
48:1551:101492:11:12:89:524:189:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Madrian, and Metrick (2002) examined large samples of employee administrative data from two firms, one 
48:1552:101595:12:11:89:524:177:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:that introduced a match of 25 percent up to 4 percent of pay and another that held the match rate constant 
48:1553:101702:11:12:89:524:166:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:but increased the match cap.  Their reduced-form estimates were not inconsistent with a relatively moderate 
48:1554:101810:12:11:89:524:154:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:substitution effect and a very small income effect.  Copeland and VanDerhei (2001) estimated the impact of 
48:1555:101917:11:12:89:527:143:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:match  rates  and  caps  using  a  reduced-form  sequential-response  regression  model  for  137  matching  
48:1556:102026:12:11:89:526:131:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:formulas  and  a  very  large  sample  of  participants,  in  which  a  separate  equation  was  estimated  for  each  
48:1557:102145:11:12:89:527:120:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:match  rate  the  participant  faced.    They,  too,  found  evidence  that  matching  raised  participation  and  
48:1558:102260:12:11:89:526:108:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:contributions.    Probably  the  biggest  difference  between  these  studies  and  the  current  paper  is  that  the  
48:1559:102380:11:12:89:524:97:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:analysis below is based on a life-cycle-consistent empirical specification, constructs the household’s budget 
48:1560:102490:12:11:89:525:85:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:set  (rather  than  the  employee),  and  incorporates  virtual  income  into  the  estimation.  A  companion  paper,  
48:1561:102609:11:0:89:443:74:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:Engelhardt and Kumar (2003), provided a further discussion of the previous literature.   
49:1562:102700:0:18:247:539:705:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:)1/()1)(1)(1(12FVFrmθθ−++−−,      from      matchQ      to      maxQ,      the      slope      is      
49:1563:102803:18:17:207:524:687:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:A:)1/()1)(1(12FFrθθ−+−−, and beyond maxQ, the slope is zero.  At the match cap, matchQ, 
49:1564:102889:17:14:89:372:670:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:there is a kink point, k, at which the match is exhausted.   
49:1565:102950:14:14:125:528:656:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:A:The  introduction  of  the  employer  match  with  a  cap  has  differential  effects  
49:1566:103037:14:13:89:526:642:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:depending  upon  the  location  on  the  budget  set.    For  low  levels  of  contributions,  the  
49:1567:103137:13:14:89:526:629:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:budget  set  rotates  outward,  and  there  are  opposing  income  and  substitution  effects,  but  
49:1568:103238:14:14:89:525:615:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:for higher levels of contributions, the budget set shifts out in parallel, and there is only an 
49:1569:103334:14:16:89:533:601:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:income   effect,   for   which   contributions   fall   with   the   imposition   of   the   match.      
49:1570:103439:16:14:89:526:585:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:Furthermore,  once  the  match  cap  is  in  place,  changes  in  the  match  rate,  Vm,  may  not  
49:1571:103539:14:14:90:527:571:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:induce  changes  in  contributions  if  individuals  are  bunched  at  the  kink  point,  k,  and  
49:1572:103638:14:14:90:528:557:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:standard  income  and  substitution  effects  are  not  well  defined.      Instead,  income  and  
49:1573:103737:14:15:90:525:543:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:substitution effects on each budget segment are defined by the slopes given above and the 
49:1574:103827:15:19:90:397:528:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:virtual incomes shown in the figure, 1vy and 2vy, respectively.  
49:1575:103892:19:13:90:93:509:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C: 
49:1576:103892:13:14:126:528:496:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:A:By  specifying  a  detailed  theoretical  framework,  this  paper  represents  a  stark  
49:1577:103981:14:14:89:526:482:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:departure  from  the  previous  literature.    There  were  eight  criteria  that  guided  the  model  
49:1578:104084:14:14:89:529:468:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:detailed  below.    First,  it  should  incorporate  non-linear  budget  sets  explicitly.    In  
49:1579:104182:14:14:89:526:454:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:particular,  the  budget  sets  individuals  actually  face  are  substantially  more  complicated  
49:1580:104282:14:13:90:522:440:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:than the ones depicted in Figure 1, because they may have multiple kinks due to variable-
49:1581:104371:13:14:90:526:427:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:rate  matches,  and  there  may  be  multiple  kinks  because  there  are  multiple  marginal  tax  
49:1582:104471:14:14:90:525:413:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:rates, and contributions are tax-deductible, so that making a contribution may change the 
49:1583:104561:14:14:90:524:399:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:marginal tax rate.  Surprisingly, none of the previous studies even have accounted for the 
49:1584:104652:14:13:90:526:385:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:effect  of  taxation  on  401(k)  saving.    Second  and  third,  respectively,  the  model  should  
49:1585:104753:13:14:90:527:372:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:allow  for  goods  other  than  consumption,  such  as  leisure,  that  enter  utility—because  a  
49:1586:104852:14:14:90:526:358:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:change  in  the  match  rate  may  induce  intratemporal  substitution  across  goods—and  for  
49:1587:104948:14:14:90:525:344:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:uncertain lifetimes and bequests, facets that are important to individuals of the ages found 
49:1588:105041:14:14:90:526:330:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:in  the  HRS.    Fourth,  the  model  should  allow  for  wealth  accumulation  in  many  forms,

50:1611:107214:14:14:89:525:667:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f3:B:for an optimal asset location decision, whereby the consumer must decide which assets to

58:2198:132167:14:14:275:339:667:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:C:Appendix B 
58:2199:132178:14:14:90:93:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
58:2200:132178:14:13:126:525:639:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:This appendix describes the construction of and gives background on the analysis 
58:2201:132259:13:14:90:370:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:dataset.  Additional detail can be provided upon request.   
58:2202:132319:14:14:126:129:612:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
58:2203:132319:14:14:126:527:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:The  sample  consists  of  1,042  individuals  from  wave  1  of  the  HRS  who  were  
58:2204:132406:14:14:90:526:584:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employed  in  1991,  eligible  for  a  401(k),  whose  employer  provided  a  SPD  for  the  plan,  
58:2205:132506:14:13:90:529:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and  who  had  linked  administrative  W-2  and  Social  Security  earnings  data.    The  
58:2206:132597:13:14:90:526:557:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f6:B:restricted-access  employer-provided  SPDs  are  distributed  as  the  HRS  Wave  1  Pension  
58:2207:132691:14:14:90:525:543:144:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:B:Plan Detail Data Set (Gustman, Mitchell, Samwick, and Steinmeier, 1999).  This dataset 
58:2208:132778:14:14:90:530:529:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contains   plan   type,   eligibility   rules,   benefit   formulae,   employer   contribution   and   
58:2209:132881:14:14:90:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:matching formulae, early and normal retirement dates, and other information described in 
58:2210:132970:14:13:90:525:501:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the SPD, but not any information for individual employees.  The W-2 data are distributed 
58:2211:133059:13:14:90:528:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f6:B:as  the  HRS  Wages  and  Self-Employment  Income  in  Covered  and  Non-Covered  Jobs  
58:2212:133147:14:14:90:526:474:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:dataset (Mitchell, Olson, and Steinmeier, 1996).  The dataset is a cross-section for 1991 
58:2213:133237:14:14:90:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:because even though there are earnings and deferral data prior to 1991, there are no data 
58:2214:133327:14:14:90:529:446:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:on  other  income  and  wealth  needed  to  construct  full  income  prior  to  1991  in  the  HRS.    
58:2215:133430:14:13:90:526:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Some of the individuals in the sample worked in 1991 but were retired at the time of the 
58:2216:133519:13:14:90:525:419:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:first  interview  in  1992.    Exclusion  of  these  individuals  had  no  impact  on  the  estimation  
58:2217:133623:14:14:90:139:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:results.   
58:2218:133633:14:14:125:128:391:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
58:2219:133633:14:14:125:521:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:There  are  four  types  of  employer  matching:  fixed-rate,  discretionary,  profit-
58:2220:133719:14:13:90:526:363:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sharing,  and  variable-rate  matching.    Engelhardt  and  Kumar  (2003)  discussed  these  in  
58:2221:133816:13:14:90:526:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:detail.    Because  the  extent  of  matching  is  not  always  known  in  advance  to  employees  
58:2222:133915:14:14:90:525:336:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:making deferral decisions in profit-sharing and discretionary plans, these plans were not 
58:2223:134005:14:14:90:527:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:included  in  our  sample.    The  SPDs  were  used  to  construct  the  complete  schedule  of  
58:2224:134102:14:13:90:528:308:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer  matching  contributions  for  each  individual  in  our  sample  and  applied  all  
58:2225:134196:13:14:90:525:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:relevant  restrictions  on  plan  eligibility  in  the  SPD,  including  those  due  to  tenure,  hours,  
58:2226:134302:14:14:90:419:281:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:earnings, age, and vesting of the employer matching contributions.   
58:2227:134371:14:14:90:93:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
58:2228:134371:14:14:126:527:253:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Because  workers’  budget  sets  can  have  multiple  kinks  and,  therefore,  multiple  
58:2229:134460:14:14:90:525:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:points  of  non-differentiability,  from  changes  in  match  and  marginal  tax  rates,  a  smooth,  
58:2230:134562:14:13:90:530:225:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:differentiable   budget   set   around   all   kink   points   was   constructed,   following   the   
58:2231:134664:13:14:90:525:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:methodology of MaCurdy, Green, and Paarsch (1990).  Specifically, kernel regression of 
58:2232:134751:14:14:90:525:198:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the implicit subsidy from employer matching and tax deductibility on the set of potential 
58:2233:134841:14:14:90:528:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:contributions  from  0  to  $9500  (the  federal  maximum  contribution  in  1991)  by  $50  
58:2234:134934:14:12:90:532:170:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:increments   was   used   to   smooth   the   budget   set,   using   the   Gaussian   kernel,   
58:2235:135031:12:19:191:532:158:49:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:2/2)2/1()(zezK−=π,    with    bandwidth    chosen    by    Silverman’s    rule    of    thumb,    
58:2236:135129:19:8:153:243:139:49:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:5/1/9.0nmh=, where )349.1/,varmin(
58:2237:135163:8:16:290:525:131:49:g_d0_f6:144:g_d0_f3:A:xxiqrm= and iqrx is the inter-quartile range.   A 
58:2238:135213:16:13:89:526:115:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:smooth  marginal  implicit  subsidy  function  was  constructed  from  the  kernel-regression  
58:2239:135308:13:14:89:525:102:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:estimates.  The respondent-reported income in wave 1 of the HRS referred to behavior in 
58:2240:135396:14:0:89:526:88:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:calendar year 1991; hence, AΔ was formed by using taxable wealth in 1992 taken from 
59:2241:135482:0:16:90:527:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:wave  1,  taxable  wealth  in  1991,  which  was  capitalized  from  1991  capital  income,  a  
59:2242:135578:16:14:90:522:692:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:technique  is  commonly  used  in  the  literature,  and  TAR  constructed  from  a  weighted-
59:2243:135672:14:15:89:525:678:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:average gross return based on returns in Ibbotson (2003).  Tax rules from 1991 were used 
59:2244:135761:15:22:89:524:663:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:to construct an IRA phase-out calculator to determine ζ and lyζ, and household income, 
59:2245:135848:22:14:90:524:641:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:tax, and demographic data and NBER’s TAXSIM calculator (Feenberg and Coutts, 1993) 
59:2246:135931:14:13:90:527:627:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:were  used  to  construct  marginal  tax  rates  and  taxes  paid  for  each  household.    The  
59:2247:136028:13:14:90:527:614:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:estimated  kernel-regression  function  was  numerically  integrated  to  obtain  the  dollar  
59:2248:136123:14:14:90:526:600:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:amount  of  implicit  subsidy  for  every  level  of  potential  401(k)  contribution,  which,  with  
59:2249:136225:14:14:90:526:586:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:full  income,  was  used  to  construct  virtual  full  income  along  all  portions  of  the  budget  
59:2250:136328:14:14:90:123:572:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sets.    
59:2251:136337:14:13:126:129:558:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
59:2252:136337:13:15:126:526:545:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:For  the  private  and  public  pension  components  in  ω  in  (18),  individuals  were  
59:2253:136427:15:13:89:528:530:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:divided  into  cells  based  on  exogenous  demographic  characteristics  and  the  Social  
59:2254:136519:13:14:89:527:517:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Security  covered  earnings  from  1951-1991  and  W-2  earnings  records  from  1980-1991

59:2259:136997:22:16:90:528:433:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:into  the  HRS  DC/401(k)  Calculator  (Engelhardt,  2004)  developed  to  calculate  for  
59:2260:137088:16:15:90:521:417:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:individuals  with  defined  contribution  plans  their  DC  pension  wealth,  DCW,  non-

59:2271:137551:22:11:89:527:316:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:calculator  developed  by  Coile  and  Gruber  (2000)  to  calculate  Social  Security  wealth,  
59:2272:137648:11:10:103:441:305:49:g_d0_f6:49:g_d0_f6:F:SSW,  accrual,  SSα,  and  change  in  accrual  for  additional  earnings,  SS

59:2275:137844:22:14:90:526:255:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:calculated assuming a 401(k) contribution of 50 dollars for all individuals (regardless of

59:2277:137965:14:13:90:93:227:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
59:2278:137965:13:14:126:527:214:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:Finally,  the  sample  is  likely  non-random  because  it  is  based  on  individuals  for  
59:2279:138058:14:14:90:525:200:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:whom the HRS was able to obtain 1) an employer-provided SPD for the 401(k) plan, and 
59:2280:138143:14:14:90:525:186:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:2) permission from the individual to match SSA covered earnings and IRS W-2 earnings 
59:2281:138228:14:14:90:526:172:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:histories.    To  understand  the  exclusion  restrictions  that  were  developed,  it  is  useful  to  
59:2282:138332:14:13:90:528:158:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:note  the  manner  in  which  the  HRS  obtained  the  SPDs  and  administrative  earnings  data.    
59:2283:138433:13:14:90:524:145:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:The HRS asked all respondents who reported being in a (current or past) pension-covered 
59:2284:138521:14:14:90:529:131:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:job  to  provide  the  name  and  address  of  the  employer.    To  maintain  respondent  
59:2285:138612:14:14:90:526:117:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:confidentiality,  the  HRS  attempted  to  contact  the  employer,  not  about  the  respondent’s  
59:2286:138711:14:14:90:525:103:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:pension(s), but more generally as part of a survey of pension providers in which the HRS 
59:2287:138800:14:13:90:527:89:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:requested  copies  of  SPDs  for  the  universe  of  pensions  the  employer  provided  (to  all  
59:2288:138898:13:0:90:526:76:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employees).    The  HRS  then  “matched”  from  this  universe  the  appropriate  pension(s)  to  
60:2289:138998:0:13:90:524:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the respondent based on the respondent’s characteristics, e.g., union status, method of pay 
60:2290:139090:13:14:90:526:695:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:(hourly,  salaried,  commission,  piece  rate),  occupation,  tenure,  etc.      The  “match”  rates  
60:2291:139192:14:14:90:525:681:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:were  well  below  100  percent:  65  percent  of  those  currently  working  in  pension-covered  
60:2292:139291:14:14:90:526:667:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:jobs, 66 percent for the last job for those not working, and 35 percent for jobs held five 
60:2293:139382:14:14:90:467:653:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:years or longer prior to the current (last) job for those working (not working).  
60:2294:139464:14:13:125:128:639:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
60:2295:139464:13:14:125:526:626:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:There  are  a  number  of  important  reasons  for  the  failure  to  match  an  SPD  to  the  
60:2296:139559:14:14:90:528:612:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:respondent.    First,  the  respondent  may  not  have  given  correct  employer  name  and  
60:2297:139652:14:14:90:525:598:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:address.  Second, the HRS may have failed to receive the SPD because the employer may 
60:2298:139738:14:14:90:527:584:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:have  refused  to  comply  with  the  pension  provider  survey,  the  employer  could  not  be  
60:2299:139835:14:13:90:525:570:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:located at the address given, or the employer went out of business or merged with another 
60:2300:139925:13:14:90:527:557:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:company  and  no  longer  existed  under  the  name  given  by  the  respondent.    Third,  the  
60:2301:140022:14:14:90:525:543:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer may have submitted an SPD, but the HRS was unable to match the SPD to the 
60:2302:140105:14:14:90:526:529:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:respondent  based  on  the  plan  detail  and  the  respondent’s  characteristics.    This  is  less  
60:2303:140207:14:14:90:525:515:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:likely for union and public sector workers, who are easy to identify and whose plans are 
60:2304:140296:14:13:90:525:501:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:easy to obtain, and more likely for workers whose employers had undergone mergers and 
60:2305:140382:13:14:90:333:488:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:acquisitions with subsequent plan modifications.   
60:2306:140433:14:14:126:129:474:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A: 
60:2307:140433:14:14:90:525:460:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: The exclusion restrictions were constructed as follows.  First, Form 5500 data for 
60:2308:140516:14:14:90:525:446:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:1988-1992 from the Department of Labor, Employee Benefit Security Administration, on 
60:2309:140601:14:13:90:527:432:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  universe  of  pension  plans  with  100  or  more  participants  and  a  5  percent  random  
60:2310:140699:13:14:89:527:419:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:sample  of  plans  with  less  than  100  participants  were  obtained.    Second,  plans  were  
60:2311:140796:14:14:89:527:405:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:divided  into  cells  defined  by  Census  region,  employment  size  category,  one-digit  SIC  
60:2312:140893:14:14:90:525:391:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:code,  year,  and  union  status  (union  plan  vs.  non-union  plan).    The  first  exclusion  is  the  
60:2313:140999:14:14:90:525:377:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:incidence of pension plan outsourcing by cell in 1992, where outsourcing means the plan 
60:2314:141087:14:13:90:525:363:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:was administered by an entity other than the employer (weighted using sampling weights 
60:2315:141174:13:14:90:524:350:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:provided by DOL). The intuition here is that the HRS was less likely to have obtained an 
60:2316:141262:14:14:89:526:336:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:SPD  from  the  employer  if  (on  average  in  its  cell)  plan  administration  was  outsourced,  
60:2317:141362:14:14:89:529:322:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:because   more   than   one   contact   was   needed   (first   the   employer,   then   the   plan   
60:2318:141464:14:13:89:527:308:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:administrator)  to  have  received  the  SPD.  (It  may  well  have  been  that  plans  that  were  
60:2319:141564:13:14:89:524:295:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:outsourced were better administered and, therefore, employers that outsourced were more 
60:2320:141652:14:14:89:525:281:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:likely to have returned the pension provider survey.  However, this was likely more than 
60:2321:141741:14:14:90:525:267:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:offset  because  the  SPD  request  was  significantly  less  likely  to  have  been  fulfilled  when  
60:2322:141844:14:14:90:526:253:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:multiple  entities  needed  to  be  contacted.) The  second  exclusion  was  the  incidence  of  
60:2323:141940:14:13:89:526:239:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:pension  plan  consolidation  due  mergers  and  acquisitions  by  cell  from  1988-1992.    The  
60:2324:142038:13:14:89:526:226:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:intuition  here  is  that  the  HRS  was  less  likely  either  to  have  obtained  an  SPD  from  the  
60:2325:142142:14:14:89:525:212:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer or to have matched it to the employee if (on average in its cell) there had been a 
60:2326:142234:14:14:89:527:198:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:lot  of  plan  consolidation,  because  plan  names  and  detail  were  often  changed  upon  
60:2327:142328:14:14:89:525:184:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:consolidation.  Two other variables were used as exclusions for pensions on past jobs in 
60:2328:142417:14:13:89:527:170:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:our  selection  equations:  dummies  for  whether  the  individual  left  the  job  because  the  
60:2329:142515:13:14:89:527:157:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:business  closed  or  was  laid  off,  respectively.    These  helped  to  measure  whether  the  
60:2330:142613:14:14:89:526:143:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:employer  possibly  was  in  financial  difficulty  at  severance,  which,  if  that  resulted  in  a  
60:2331:142716:14:14:90:528:129:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:business failure, would have made it more difficult for the HRS to have obtained an SPD.   
60:2332:142807:14:14:90:93:115:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
60:2333:142807:14:14:126:526:101:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:There were three important considerations in constructing the instruments.  First, 
60:2334:142890:14:0:90:527:87:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  instruments  were  drawn  from  the  information  set  tΩ.      Because  t  is  1991,  all  
61:2335:142989:0:13:90:526:708:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:information  from  1989  and  1990  is  in  the  information  set  and  orthogonal  to  decisions  
61:2336:143088:13:17:90:525:695:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:made in 1991 under rational expectations.  Second, because the observed marginal match 
61:2337:143175:17:16:90:525:678:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:and tax rates depend upon 401(k) and IRA contributions, IRAzmzpp⋅ and kzp401 are based 
61:2338:143262:16:14:90:528:662:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:on  first-dollar  measures:  the  employer  match  on  the  first  dollar  contributed  and  the  
61:2339:143360:14:14:90:526:648:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:marginal tax rate at which the first dollar contributed is deductible (which equals the tax 
61:2340:143452:14:14:90:524:634:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rate on the last dollar of earnings).   Third, to minimize dependence on individual-specific 
61:2341:143545:14:13:90:527:620:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:income  and  family  size  that  might  be  correlated  with  saving  behavior,  the  first-dollar  
61:2342:143645:13:14:90:525:607:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:rates were calculated for a synthetic individual of each marital status assumed to have no 
61:2343:143736:14:14:90:527:593:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:capital  income,  no  children,  under  age  65,  and  taking  the  standard  deduction—where  
61:2344:143831:14:14:90:524:579:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:marital status is assumed exogenous—with synthetic annual labor earnings constructed as 
61:2345:143919:14:14:90:531:565:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:follows:   individuals   were   divided   into   cells   based   on   exogenous   demographic   
61:2346:144015:14:19:90:525:551:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:characteristics, and the cell mean gross hourly wage rate, 2−•tw, was multiplied by 2,000 
61:2347:144105:19:14:90:525:532:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:annual  hours,  H.  Let the subscript • denote a synthetic measure and the superscript 0 
61:2348:144194:14:17:90:260:518:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:denote a first-dollar measure, then

61:2352:144490:24:16:90:356:434:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:where IRAQ was set to one dollar for all individuals.     
61:2353:144548:16:14:90:93:418:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B: 
61:2354:144548:14:19:126:527:404:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:It  is  important  to  note  that  the  tax  function  for  pΔ  in  the  endogenous  variable  
61:2355:144643:19:16:148:525:385:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:A:)ln(/ωvypΔ, is based on the tax system in 1991, but the tax function for the instruments 
61:2356:144732:16:14:89:524:369:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:is different because it is based on the tax system in 1989 (indicated by the subscript 2−t 
61:2357:144822:14:14:89:525:355:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:in (B.2)-(B.3) above).  Figure 2 plots the federal marginal tax rate by real AGI (in 1991 
61:2358:144912:14:13:89:526:341:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:dollars)  for  a  single  individual  under  65  in  1989  and  1991.    For  individuals  with  AGI  
61:2359:145014:13:14:89:527:328:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:below  $50,000,  the  functions  are  essentially  the  same,  but  differ  for  those  above  this  
61:2360:145115:14:14:89:525:314:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:level.  Specifically, above this income level in 1989, the marginal tax rate increased from 
61:2361:145207:14:14:89:525:300:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:28  to  33  percent  due  to  the  phase-out  of  the  personal  exemption.    However,  the  Budget  
61:2362:145309:14:14:89:526:286:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:Act of 1990 raised the top marginal tax rate to 31 percent and changed the phase-out of 
61:2363:145397:14:13:89:527:272:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:the  personal  exemption.    Therefore,  the  non-linearity  in  the  instruments’  tax  function  
61:2364:145496:13:14:90:525:259:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:differs from that for the endogenous regressor due to the tax-law change, which is taken 
61:2365:145585:14:14:90:527:245:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:as  exogenous  to  the  individual.      About  15  percent  of  the  sample  is  affected  by  this  
61:2366:145687:14:14:90:309:231:144:g_d0_f3:144:g_d0_f3:B:differential non-linearity in the instruments.
